Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe seven worlds praise (Sud─Бsa) as if he were Indra; him whose fame (spreads) through thespacious heaven and earth; who, munificent, has distributed (wealth) on every eminent person n, and (for him) theflowing (rivers) have destroyed Yudhyamadhi in war.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He whose fame the Apportioner has apportioned to every head between the two wide world-halves,
they hymn (him) just as the seven streams do Indra. He тАЬwhetted
downтАЭ Yudhy─Бmadhi at the moment of encounter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ┼Ыr├бvas- in p─Бda a echoes the one in 23d.

Geldner, flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa., takes ab as separate clauses, supplying тАЬ(sich ausbreitet)тАЭ as the verb in p─Бda a. This is unnecessary: the hemistich can be a single clause, with the accent on vibabh─Б╠Бj─Б in b conditioned by the rel. y├бsya in a. (Geldner considers this possibility in n. 24ab.) K├╝mmel (333) also follows the single clause interpr.

Note the lengthened 3rd sg. pf. ending in babh─Б╠Бj─Б, guaranteed (and required) by the cadence. On lengthening of the pf. endings see the brief remarks by K├╝mmel (42), though without any indication of the relative frequency; it is my impression that lengthening of the 1st/3rd sg. -a is quite rare in the RV, but I havenтАЩt made a count.

The fame being distributed is presumably that of Sud─Бs, though covertly assimiliated to IndraтАЩs; note the explicit comparison of the praise he receives to IndraтАЩs in the simile in c. The ─Бmreс╕Нita тАЬevery headтАЭ (┼Ы─лrс╣гс╣З├й-┼Ы─лrс╣гс╣Зe) must refer to every person, or rather every person eligible for fame (excluding women and nonelite males), in Sud─БsтАЩs entourage: they all get a piece of the fame-pie that he acquired by himself. The geographical extravagance of тАЬevery head between the two wide world halvesтАЭ – that is, every eligible person on earth – is presumably part of a totalizing claim about the outcome of the Ten KingsтАЩ Battle, that the whole world was brought under Sud─БsтАЩs sway. 14 The loud sound of rivers in flood is the point of the comparison in c. One of the words for тАШriverтАЩ, nad─л╠Б, is folk etymologically (and probably etymologically; see EWA s.v.) connected with тИЪnad тАШroarтАЩ, as in the explicit etymological statement in AV III.13.1 y├бd ad├бс╕е saс╣Гprayat─л╠Бr ├бh─Бv ├бnadat─Б hat├й / t├бsm─Бd ─Б╠Бnady├▓ n─Б╠Бma stha Wh тАЬSince formerly (? ad├бs) going forth together, ye resounded (nad) when the dragon was slain, therefore ye are streams (nad─л╠Б) by name.тАЭ The signature verb n├н тИЪ┼Ы─Б тАШwhet downтАЩ that we have met a number of times before (see comm. ad vs. 6) now implicitly takes Sud─Бs as its subject, as a sort of climactic usage.

The PN yudhy─Бmadh├н is obviously a speaking name, with some form of тИЪyudh тАШfightтАЩ embedded in it. See Oldenberg for various possibilites for its formation. It is tempting to see as its base a 1st pl. middle *y├║dhy─Бmahi тАЬletтАЩs fight,тАЭ with the older expected 1st pl. ending *-madhi before de-occlusion.

Griffith

Him whose fame spreads between wide earth and heaven, who, as dispenser, gives each chief his portion,
Seven flowing Rivers glorify like Indra. He slew Yudhyamadhi in close encounter.

Geldner

Dessen Ruhm zwischen den beiden Welten sich ausbreitet, der auf jeden Kopf als Verteiler die Beute verteilt hat, ihn preisen sie wie die sieben Str├╢me den Indra. Er hat den Yudhyamadhi im Zweikampf niedergestochen.

Grassmann

Dessen Ruhm sich zwischen den beiden weiten Welten verbreitet, der jedem Haupte Gaben zutheilt als Vertheiler, ihn preisen wie den Indra die sieben Str├╢me, er streckte den Judhjamadhi zu Boden im Kampfe.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, leaders (of rites), attend upon this (prince) as you did upon Divod─Бsa, the father of Sud─Бsa;favour the prayers of the devout son of Pijavana, and may his strength be unimpaired, undecaying].тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You superior men, you Maruts, accompany this (man) here, like Divod─Бsa, the father of Sud─Бs.
Give aid to the aspiration of PaijavanaтАФlordly power difficult to attain and unagingтАФ(as he) seeks (your) favor.

Griffith

Attend on him O ye heroic Maruts as on Sudas’s father Divodasa.
Further Paijavana’s desire with favour. Guard faithfully his lasting firm dominion.
